## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (deterministic rate laws / ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target is dA_dt, the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard formulation of chemical kinetics via rate-law ODEs. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are mass-action-style consumption/production terms f(A) and possibly time-varying rate coefficients f(t) due to changing conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or excess-reactant regime)
- Zero-order production/source: dA_dt = c0 (constant feed or generation term)
- First-order decay (mass action): dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Linear source–sink (CSTR/well-mixed with feed and removal): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (approach to steady state A* = c0/c1)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or recombination)
- General n-th order power law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall order / complex mechanism lumping)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium (linear driving force): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (net rate proportional to deviation from equilibrium concentration c1)
- Parallel pathways (mixed orders): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular + bimolecular consumption channels)
- Autocatalytic/branching form: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-acceleration at low A with depletion/limitation at high A)
- Time-varying first-order rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * t) * A (rate constant drifting linearly in time due to temperature/catalyst changes)
- Exponentially varying first-order rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (accelerating/decelerating effective rate constant under changing conditions)
- Periodically modulated kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * A (time-periodic forcing such as light intensity or reactor cycling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If A is being consumed irreversibly, dA_dt is typically nonpositive and often contains an overall negative sign multiplying a nonnegative function of A.
- A proportionality dA_dt ∝ -A implies a constant half-life and exponential decay; deviations from exponential curvature suggest non-first-order terms (e.g., A**2).
- Dominant A**2 (or higher) terms produce fast initial depletion at high A and strong slowing as A decreases; this often indicates bimolecular/termination steps.
- A linear form dA_dt = c0 - c1*A indicates a stable steady state at A = c0/c1; the sign of (A - c0/c1) determines whether A increases or decreases.
- A driving-force form dA_dt ∝ -(A - A_eq) is a signature of relaxation toward an equilibrium/steady concentration A_eq rather than depletion to zero.
- Mixed-order sums (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2) suggest parallel pathways; dominance can switch with concentration (linear at low A, quadratic at high A).
- Explicit time dependence in the rate coefficient (e.g., multiplying A by a function of t) suggests changing external conditions (temperature ramps, catalyst activation/deactivation, illumination schedules).
- Autocatalytic terms like A*(c1 - A) imply self-acceleration at low A and self-limitation at high A, consistent with chain-branching plus depletion or inhibitor buildup.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK9)
============================================================
GT: -c0*sqrt(A) + c1*_w*cos(log(A + c2))
Candidates evaluated: 92
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: `-0.2597*sqrt(A) + 0.9123*cos(log(A + 1))`**

This has two basis functions: `sqrt(A)` and `cos(log(A+1))`.

The key question is: can any candidate's functional form express `cos(log(A+1))`?

Let me recall important identities:
- `cos(x) = (e^(ix) + e^(-ix))/2` — but this involves complex numbers, not helpful for real-valued expressions
- `cos(log(A+1))` is an oscillatory function that cannot be expressed as polynomials, exponentials, rational functions, or logarithms

Let me check candidates that might contain `cos(log(...))` or equivalent:

**Candidate 2**: Contains `exp(c2*cos(c3*log(A*c4 + 1)))` — this is `exp(cos(log))`, not `cos(log)`. Cannot match.

**Candidate 5**: Contains `exp(c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7))`. With appropriate constants, `sin(c5*log(A*c6+1) + c7)` can become `cos(log(A+1))` by setting c5=1, c6=1, c7=π/2. But it's inside an `exp()`, giving `exp(c4*cos(log(A+1)))`. The overall structure is `rational_terms + c3*A*exp(...)/(A+c1) + c9*exp(...)/(A+c1)`. This wraps cos in exp, so it can't produce a pure cos term.

**Candidate 34**: Contains `exp(c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8 + 1) + c9))`. Same issue — cos inside exp.

**Candidate 42**: Contains `c4*exp(c5*cos(c6*log(A*c7 + 1)))` — cos inside exp again.

**Candidate 75**: `c0 + c1*log(A*c2 + c3) + c4*exp(c5*cos(c6*log(A*c7 + 1)))`. Again cos inside exp.

**Candidate 12**: Contains `c3*exp(c4*cos(c5*log(A*c6 + 1)))` — cos inside exp.

**Candidate 17**: Contains `exp(c2*cos(c3*log(A*c4 + 1)))` — cos inside exp.

None of these candidates contain a bare `cos(log(...))` term. The GT requires `cos(log(A+1))` as a basis function. Since `cos(log(A+1))` is oscillatory and cannot be represented by:
- Polynomials, rational functions
- Exponentials `exp(A*c)`
- Logarithms `log(...)`
- `sqrt(A)`, power functions
- `exp(cos(log(...)))` (this is fundamentally different from `cos(log(...))`)

None of the candidates contain the required `cos(log(A+1))` basis function in a form that could match the GT.

Let me do a final sweep for any candidate I might have missed that has a bare cosine or sine of a logarithm... No candidate has `cos(log(...))` or `sin(log(...))` as a standalone term (not wrapped in exp).
